Father and Son Commit Suicide by Poisoning Simultaneously 157

▲ Due to Difficulty Maintaining a Livelihood

▲ A Most Tragic Scene

Xu Jinmei, a local resident aged 65 who worked as a laborer for the Changxing Shipping Company at 4 Wuma Road, has been out of work for more than six months. His eldest son, Yongnian, aged 31, who used to work for Changxing and other firms, has also been laid off for seven months. His youngest son, Yonghuan, aged 26, works as a chauffeur for the Xinchang Transportation Company at Tianfei Palace Bridge, earning only a few dozen yuan per month. The entire family relies on him to make ends meet, but it is difficult to support them, leading to mounting debts. Xu and his eldest son, Yongnian, considered the situation and saw no way out. As a result, they both decided that it would be better to leave this world early to reduce Yonghuan's burden. So, they resolved to commit suicide. Yesterday morning, the father and son purchased opium paste. Soon after, they both became poisoned and were beyond help. Their youngest son, Yonghuan, rushed them to Tongren Hospital for treatment. It is said that they ingested too much poison, and their lives are in danger.

Undutiful Son Shoots His Elderly Father for Inheritance 158

▲ Three Shots Fired, Luckily None Hit

Gu Lanzhou, a farmer residing at 11 Yanjia Bridge, Hongqiao Road, West Shanghai, is 45 years old and comes from a well-to-do family. He has two sons, Baogen, 25, and Amao, 20, both of whom are married. Last spring, all the family property was divided into three shares by the local village head Chen Yixiang (one share for Lanzhou and his wife, and one share each for Baogen and Amao), and each established their own household. However, Baogen did not engage in proper work and spent his time wandering around. Lanzhou repeatedly admonished him, but to no avail. As a result, the property he received was sold off within two years. Yesterday afternoon around 4 p.m., Baogen forcibly demanded land deeds from his father but was refused. He pulled out a gun and fired three shots at his father, but luckily none hit. Lanzhou was terrified and cried for help. Neighbors heard the cries and came to the rescue, saving him from danger. He then reported the incident to the Chengjia Bridge Police Station. Police Chief Lu Peiyu received the report and personally led officers to arrest the undutiful son Gu Baogen and escort him to the First Sub-bureau of the Sixth District. However, the handgun had already been discarded and could not be found. After a brief interrogation by Chief Bi, the case was deemed significant, and a written report was prepared to be sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for strict handling today.

Invoices Must Include the Year 159

▲ Otherwise, They Will Be Considered as Failing to Affix Stamp Tax

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various trade associations stating that the Rice Trade Association had reported that Longxingtai was fined for failing to affix stamp tax on an invoice, and requested that the fine be revoked. The letter stated that the invoices in question, when inspected by the designated personnel, all indicated the price of the goods, the brand of the recipient, and were stamped with the store's seal. However, they did not include the year above the month and day. The phrase "last year" was considered definitive proof of the year. The bureau has found that invoices without the year are common in all industries and are inevitably used as a way to avoid stamp tax. To prevent people from evading tax and to avoid setting a precedent for others to follow, the bureau had no choice but to impose a discretionary fine. Therefore, the Chamber of Commerce should inform all businesses that when issuing invoices and receipts, they must not change the format and must include the year for easy identification during inspections. If anyone deliberately tries to be cunning and is caught, it will be considered tax evasion and no exceptions will be made.

Firecrackers Explode, Collapsing Kitchen Shed 160

▲ Twelve-Year-Old Boy Seriously Injured

The Yingfeng Rice Store at 160 Meiyuan Road, Zhabei, owned by Mr. Zhi Xu (30 years old) from Yangzhou, was doing a decent business. Recently, to save money, they sublet the kitchen shed at the back to a Mr. Su from Funing. Su then sublet it to Guo Zhenxiang from Yancheng, who made firecrackers at a thatched house on Guangzhao Road, as a place to store goods. Unexpectedly, at 0:10 a.m. yesterday, Guo was careless when moving the firecrackers, and they suddenly collapsed, pressing on the gunpowder placed nearby. A deafening explosion occurred, shaking the building, and the kitchen shed collapsed instantly. Guo was caught in the blast, his face was severely burned, and he lost his sight. At the same time, a twelve-year-old boy named Da Maozi, son of Mr. Su, also suffered severe head injuries. After the accident, police officers Wang Yuanji and Shi Yunpeng from posts 67 in the 2nd sub-district of the 4th district, rushed to the scene upon hearing the explosion. They managed to send the injured Guo Zhenxiang and the boy Da Maozi to the hospital for treatment, and took Mr. Zhi Xu into custody. After questioning him, Chief He deemed it a case of injury and sent him to the bureau for further investigation. It is reported that Guo's injuries are severe, and although his life is not in danger, he may become disabled. It is also reported that Mr. Su has fled and is being pursued by the police.

Three Puppets, Two Jars of Water 161

▲ Used as Tools for Extorting Money

▲ Arrested and Sent for Investigation

Shen Jinfu, the owner of a certain carriage shop at 295 Meibai Ge Road, recently came up with an unconventional idea. He gathered Gao Hanqing and women Shen Yinshi and Wu Shenshi, and set up three puppets and two jars of water in the carriage shop. Shen Jinfu also claimed that the gods would take turns possessing him, and that when possessed, all requests would be granted without fail. As a result, foolish men and women who believed in divine power went to seek divine guidance and fortune-telling. Over time, the number of seekers increased, and the place became as busy as a marketplace. Seeing that this method of extorting money was very easy, Shen and others stipulated that the time for divine possession would be from 4 p.m. to 6 p.m. and from 8 p.m. to 10 p.m. daily, and they would not receive anyone after the deadline. They charged one corner for those seeking divine guidance and two yuan for those seeking a divine child. As a result, the flow of people seeking wealth was overwhelming. The police learned about this and, considering it to be fraud under the guise of divine power and a violation of the prohibition order, sent undercover agents disguised as those seeking divination to investigate. After confirming the facts, Luo Biesheng, the Western Detective Chief of the Xinzha Police Station, led detectives to the location, arrested Shen, Gao, and the two women, and sent them to the First Special District Local Court. Judge Shang Feng reviewed the case, and the police lawyer Qian Mingchen clarified the circumstances of the case, requesting that they be charged with inciting and defrauding. Judge Cheng then questioned each of the defendants one by one, ordered Shen and Gao to be detained, and released the two women on bail, pending further investigation. The puppets were immediately destroyed.

Pledging a Diamond Ring in a Desperate Gamble 162

▲ Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment After Interrogation

Ma Qin, a Cantonese native, worked as a partner in a jewelry store owned by his fellow townsman Beng Chongshan at 986 Wusong Road. On the morning of the 7th of this month, he was entrusted by Cai to have a diamond ring worth 300 yuan remade. Ma, who had recently become addicted to gambling and was heavily in debt, had a greedy impulse when he saw the valuable item. He secretly took it out and pawned it at the Baohe Pawnshop at 1338 North Sichuan Road for 110 yuan, going to a gambling den for a desperate gamble. However, his luck ran out, and he quickly lost everything. Unable to make amends, he sent a letter to Cai, saying that he would temporarily return to his hometown to find a way to repay the debt. Cai, suspecting that he would not return and was hiding in Shanghai, reported the incident to the Hongkou Police Station. The Cantonese detectives Feng Qi and He Ruirui were patrolling North Sichuan Road on the evening of the 10th when they recognized Ma walking with his head down. They immediately arrested him and brought him to the police station. They found the original pawn ticket during the search and notified Cai to redeem the ring from the pawnshop. The next morning, they escorted Ma to the First Special Committee's First Court. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that the defendant Ma Qin had falsely accused residents of theft, hoping to get a reward. He presented the recovered ring and the letter to the court for investigation. Cai Chongshan then testified to the circumstances of the case. When questioned, the defendant confessed that he had been momentarily confused and pawned the diamond ring in the gambling den and lost. He pleaded for leniency. Judge Xiao Xiefen reviewed the confession and sentenced Ma Qin to six months imprisonment as a warning.

Falsely Accusing Someone of Theft to Obtain a Reward 163

▲ Chen A'si's Deceit is Excessive

▲ Sentenced to Four Months Imprisonment After Interrogation

At 9:30 a.m. on the 15th of this month, the Wang family at 254 Donghan Bile Road was robbed of valuables worth several hundred yuan, and the thieves left without a trace. At 8 p.m., Chen A'si, a native of Yangzhou, reported to Chinese detective Li Hongsheng of the Huishan Police Station that the robbers were drinking tea at a small teahouse on Yuezhou Road, and requested that they be arrested immediately. Detective Li then went to the teahouse with detective Qi Mengqing and arrested four men from Jiangbei: Wu Kaiqun, Wu Kailin, Wu Shiquan, and Wang Xiaosanzi. After questioning, it was revealed that they were not the robbers in the case, but that Chen A'si had falsely accused them in order to claim a reward. Chen claimed that Wang Xiaosanzi had reported to him. When Wang was questioned, he denied it. The detectives accompanied the victim to the police station, but he stated that none of them were the robbers. The police chief detained Chen and Wang and released the three Wus. The next morning, they were sent to the First Court of the First District. The police representative, lawyer Zhang Tianyin, stated that the defendant Chen A'si had falsely accused residents of theft, hoping to get a reward. He claimed that Wang Xiaosanzi had reported to him at 8 a.m. that morning, but the robbery on Donghan Bile Road had not yet occurred at that time. Therefore, he requested that the court release Wang. Wu Kaiqun and the other two testified that Wang Xiaosanzi had invited them to the teahouse to help resolve a money dispute, and soon after, Chen A'si arrived with the police officers and arrested them along with Wang. They knew nothing about the robbery. When questioned, Chen A'si's testimony was evasive. Wang Xiaosanzi testified that he had known the three witnesses for many years. At that time, Chen A'si asked him to invite them to the teahouse to help him collect 20 yuan from someone. Shortly after, police officers arrived and arrested them, and he did not report to them that the robbers were the three Wus. Judge judged that Chen A'si was sentenced to four months imprisonment, and Wang Xiaosanzi was acquitted.

Zhengua Factory's Purchase of Peppermint Oil Raw Materials Leads to Litigation 164

Zhu Jiliang, the general manager of Shanghai Zhenhua Peppermint Manufacturing Factory, sent Li Qianwan, the factory manager, to Ji'an, Jiangxi, in the autumn of last year to purchase raw materials for making peppermint oil. Li signed a consignment contract with Liu Youdao, the representative of the local Gongping Company, and Wang Rongbao of the Shengji Company. The contract stipulated a price limit, with Gongping consigning 6,000 catties and Shengji consigning 3,000 catties. In addition to the silver taels of deposit paid to Gongping at the time, he also gave a promissory note for 24,000 taels of silver. The remaining payment would be settled after the goods were transported to Shanghai. Later, the two companies sent Liu and Wang to Shanghai to escort the goods, but Zhenhua did not pick them up for a long time, and the promissory notes were not cashed when they matured. As a result, Gongping was owed 86,300 yuan, and Shengji was owed 36,000 yuan. Repeated demands were ignored. As the lunar new year was approaching, the two companies' representatives hired lawyers Ji Feng and Zhan Yigang to file a lawsuit against Zhu Jiliang, the general manager of Zhenhua, and Li Qianwan, the manager, requesting a court order to deliver the goods and pay the arrears, as well as interest for the delay. During the previous hearing at the First Special District Local Court, Zhu was also suing Li Qianwan in the Shanghai Local Court for secretly stealing the seal. Li was detained and unable to attend court, so the hearing was temporarily postponed. The day before yesterday, Judge Li Mo continued the trial, and Li Qianwan also appeared in court to confront the charges. The two plaintiffs first stated the circumstances of the contract with Li and presented the invoices. When questioned, the defendant Zhu Jiliang said that the Zhenhua factory's capital was only 20,000 taels of silver, so how could it handle goods worth 100,000 taels? Therefore, when he sent Li to Ji'an, he instructed him to purchase spot goods with cash, and did not order him to sign a contract with the plaintiffs. Li Qianwan then stated that although the factory's capital was only 20,000 taels, Zhu had publicly undertaken the responsibility of advancing funds for future purchases when the factory was established. The contract signed with the plaintiffs was drafted by Zhu's accountant in Zhu's office, so how could he deny it? The amount claimed by the two plaintiffs was accurate. The plaintiff's lawyer Zhan Jifeng presented letters and telegrams to prove that Zhu Jiliang had commissioned Li to purchase goods in Jiangxi. The defendant Zhu Jiliang's lawyer, Lu Dingkui, also presented a telegram draft book as evidence to the contrary. Judge Li then ordered the defendant to present the original telegram for verification, but Zhu claimed that the original telegram and other important items such as the factory's seal had been stolen by Li. Upon hearing this, Li firmly denied it. As a result, Judge Li returned all the evidence presented by both parties and instructed the lawyers to number each piece of evidence, provide an explanation, and submit a separate statement for a hearing and debate to be scheduled for a later date for review and judgment.

Woman Embezzles Large Fortune 165

▲ Uncle Files Criminal Complaint

The late Yangzhou native Shen Shaoquan had previously held important positions in the Ministry of Finance and the Hubei Salt Transportation Bureau. In the spring of the 18th year of the Republic of China, Shen Shaoquan suffered the pain of losing his wife and lived alone and listlessly. At that time, a woman named Fu Shaoqing was teaching at Shaoquan's younger brother Zhichuan's home. Zhichuan was a young man who had served in the military and in salt affairs. The brothers had always lived together and were very harmonious. Soon after, Shaoquan and Fu developed a romantic relationship and began to live together. At that time, Shaoquan's mother was still alive and strongly disapproved of this. Shaoquan also feared public opinion and brought Fu to Shanghai to live. In the winter of that year, Shaoquan died of illness in Shanghai. Zhichuan was living in Yangzhou at the time and rushed to Shanghai upon hearing the news. He found that the coffin was already in the hall. He inspected the deeds of the joint property that Shaoquan had managed during his lifetime, but unexpectedly, they were all hidden by Fu. Zhichuan demanded them from her, but Fu claimed that she would inspect them after the funeral. After the funeral, she still procrastinated. At that time, Zhichuan's mother was critically ill in Yangzhou and sent a telegram summoning him. Zhichuan hastily returned to Yangzhou. Not long after, he was in mourning. Fu took this opportunity to use a large amount of the bank deposits and transferred the remaining balance to her own account, amounting to more than 300,000. Zhichuan came to Shanghai, but his attempts to negotiate were ineffective. He hired lawyers Li Chi, Zhang Bingjun, and Ouyang Yuan to file a criminal complaint for embezzlement. Yesterday, Judge Ma of the Second Special District Local Court of Shanghai opened a hearing and ordered the defendant Fu Shaoqing to post a bond of 30,000 yuan and scheduled another hearing for a later date.

Reader Correspondence

Abolish Party Rule 173

— Wang Jiguo

Past warlord governments, of course, did not allow us common people to participate in politics, but nominally there were always formal elected members to decorate the facade of a democratic country. Unfortunately, since the revolutionary Kuomintang shouted the slogan of "ruling the country by the party," not only has the form been abolished, but the people have been more obviously excluded from politics. It seems that reading about doctrines every day has made them forget the meaning of civil rights. We are not against seeking China's progress under the leadership of the party, but we are against using the slogan of "ruling by the party" to deprive the people of their due rights. Look at the current situation, from the highest authorities to the lowest cadres, so-called chairmen and so-called committee members, apart from internal party factions, where can you find half of them that are elected by the people? Not only that, but they even shout "use party members first for employment" and "lay off non-party members when downsizing," turning the entire Republic of China into a party-ruled "Chinese Party State." Of course, there are indeed many outstanding talents within the party, but are there none outside the party? No, there are, but they are buried alive under the name of party rule. We have a painful aversion to this. Under the rule of the brutal Japanese, we were slaves and of course had no right to participate in politics, but under party rule, although we are nominally great citizens, we still have no right to participate in government. What is the difference between the two? Therefore, in order to obtain our political power, we must resist imperialist aggression externally and demand the abolition of party rule internally. In fact, as I see it, there is no such thing as party rule. Wasn't Zhang Xueliang a very powerful warlord during the Northern Expedition? What doctrines did he understand? However, he was able to transform into a deputy commander and a supervisory committee member. Wasn't Gu Weijun wanted by the National Government? However, he was able to become a revolutionary foreign minister. So-called party rule is nothing more than a tool to deprive the people of their political power and create a special privileged class. Recently, Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke and others declared that they would overthrow the dictatorship and establish a democratic government. However, examining their motives and evidence of the facts, it is nothing more than enabling a group of disgruntled party members to obtain political positions. The real masses are still excluded from politics, and talking about democracy without abolishing party rule is also a contradictory term. The current Chinese politics, although it looks like it is riddled with holes, the only key to getting to the root and source of the problem is to abolish party rule, gather talents from across the country, and organize a wise government representing the people, so that the people can express their views in politics and find a common way out. Only then can we talk about internal stability and external resistance. Finally, we solemnly declare that abolishing party rule does not fundamentally abolish the Kuomintang, but rather transforms Chinese politics from the hands of a few people to a universal development. (B)

Free Forum

"Not Removing Garden Weeds" – Zhaifu Talks

From Nanjing Road to Nanjing City (Part 1) 175

Twenty motorcycles led the way, followed by the X government's military band, the Municipal Council's military band, and finally countless (reportedly four hundred) cars, loaded with wreaths and Guo's family flags, moving down the main street slower than handcarts, while crowds of people stood by the roadside to watch… watch Guo Biao's funeral!

"Guo Biao has surpassed Huang Chu Jiu." "Not even close to Sheng Xuanhuai! Sheng Xuanhuai's funeral caused a sensation with millions of people, unprecedented in Shanghai." People on the street chatted idly.

I couldn't cross the street. I had something important to do, but Guo Biao blocked me. That dead Guo Biao actually had such power to block my way!

Unable to pass, I stood there thinking: Why wasn't the X government's military band inspiring the people to resist the enemy, but instead sending off a company boss here? If the four hundred cars and their oil were under Ma Zhanshan's command, what a huge impact would it have? Old-style funerals, though not great, gave the poor some opportunities to earn a living. Modern funerals waste oil, drain national strength, and even beggars get nothing. Whose fault is this? Guo Biao is dead, surely Guo Biao didn't leave a will insisting on doing this? Some say funerals are purely for show, to flaunt a family's wealth and power. I want to ask: If there were no audience, would there be actors? Isn't this all our fault?

Anecdotes of Mr. Qiangcun 176

— Kuang Youhan

Qiang Zhang Shu Chao, is now housed at the Huzhou Guildhall in northern Shanghai. (Ouchao is the name Mr. Qiang himself inscribed on his coffin, and the late teacher Wu Changshuo engraved the end.) Awaiting burial next year in Daocheng Mountain in Huzhou, facing his ancestors' graves. At the time of the late father's death, Mr. Qiang had a mourning couplet: "If views are the same, talented men will find peace. Sects eventually return to Baishi in old age, relying on my land. Daocheng Mountain remains unharmed. Life and death alone for the green hills."

Mr. Qiang had very close relationships with the secular Mr. Lu Daoren and his maternal uncle, Mr. Qian Taixi. Mr. Lu's poem of mourning reads: "A thousand years of heroic spirit returns. Mountains and rivers still look as they did in the past. Literature serves the country, preserving the brush. Official attire accompanies the coffin. Heaven does not begrudge the elegies left behind. People only remember the completeness of past fame. Last night, I wondered why the lamp window was dim, wanting to write a letter on fish paper, especially cold. Twenty years of patience dare not seek trust. Superfluous remarks have been repeatedly praised. Intending to write a clear history. (The public once favored me with a handwritten biography of the late Qin Guoxiang Yi.) Contemplating only proves the cause of Lacquer Garden. In life, integrity surpasses peers. The most elegant of contemporary words. If you meet the old man Wu Changshuo on the road to the underworld, you can say that you can endure hardships by wearing coarse clothes." The maternal uncle's couplet of mourning reads: "Ascend Daocheng Mountain, with Kuang Huifeng arm in arm entering the forest. Golden bones are majestic, becoming the beauty of the mountains and rivers. Leave behind traces, chasing Li Changgu, returning to simplicity. The White Jade Tower now has experienced elders."

While Mr. Qiang was ill, he orally presented a poem in the style of "Partridge Sky" to colleagues in the poetry society in the winter solstice month: "I have not done my best in loyalty and filial piety. In recent years, the ginger quilt has become less warm. Are rhinoceros horns in my eyes real or not? After death, the cowhide coat is also grateful for the favor. Ephemeral things, like water and clouds, I have put my heart and soul into being a poet. Most sad is the human world, not concluding the unfinished cause of the next life." He died five days later, alas. I respectfully filled in the original tune to mourn him. "The sight of Qionggui reminds me of what you lived for. Spring frost and autumn dew are always affectionate. Eternal remembrance is painful and hard to sleep. Embracing the green felt several times to understand. Relying on the Big Dipper, comforting the orphans. How can the stars and mountains lean to the west again. Reciting a collection of posthumous songs a thousand times, the remaining cold crickets respond to my cry."

The Grand Wind Hall's Disciples 177

— Nanxi

"Painting tigers as if hearing roaring sounds. Tears of sorrow for the times flowing horizontally. The old master's brush still lifts the cauldron. Not to mention the disciples of your family." This is a poem I gave to Zhang Shanzi from Sichuan at the He Xiangning Relief Exhibition for National Crisis. There were many works by the Zhang brothers and their disciples. The Grand Wind Hall, where Shanzi and Daqian lived, was already famous for calligraphy, painting, and seal engraving. The disciples all followed the style of Huangshan, so many outstanding talents emerged. Such as nephews Zhang Xuming, Mu Quanzong, Zhou Weixin, Hu Ruosi, Wu Zijing, Lu Yuanding, and Yan Jiquan, all were fashionable talents of the time. Xuming was not yet twenty years old. After traveling to Huangshan with Shanzi and Daqian, his sketches were numerous and exquisite, with a high and elegant realm. Daqian also sighed and added touches to them. I often think about it. Learning to paint means learning from the ancients, emphasizing copying and touching. The Grand Wind Hall has a rich collection, looking at it on all sides, resting and living there. The first thing you can't get is that. Learning from nature means emphasizing roaming. Shanzi and Daqian have traveled to Huangshan many times. Their disciples must carry staffs and food, enjoying the pleasure of children and crown clouds, exhausting the wonders of mountains, rivers, clouds, and seas. The second thing you can't get is that. Chinese calligraphy and painting share the same principles. If you can't write, you are a craftsman. Daqian came from the school of Li Meian and Zeng Nongran, and passed on the brushwork to his disciples. Many of his disciples can write Northern Stele and ancient gold inscriptions, making the calligraphy of Zeng and Li flourish in the art world. The third thing you can't get is that. Everything in the world must have a cause and effect, a source. Wagons full of millet cannot be prayed for by one pig's shoulder. The ancients emphasized inheritance, and there is a reason for it. The world is so chaotic, and many people have advocated saving the country with calligraphy and painting. Even if we retreat and talk about it, maintaining the national culture is maintaining the national character. If the national character is not extinguished, the country will not be forgotten. Calligraphers and painters, even if they cannot wield weapons to defend the country, are still better than those who wear their hair loose, wear their clothes on the left, and speak the language of the Xianbei. I write this, regretting my garrulousness.

A Silver Dollar Saved My Life 178

— Rui Yucheng

Karma is a superstition, but there is also an incredible and mysterious principle in the dark. I have personally experienced something, and now I record it as material for your research.

In the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, I served as a regimental commander in the Feng Army. One of my soldiers, named Zhong Desheng, was a bully who relied on his power. Once, he asked a poor old woman to make him a pair of shoes, agreeing on two thousand cash. After they were made, Zhong Desheng paid one yuan, and the old woman found the change for him. At that time, the money and goods were exchanged. After a while, the old woman suddenly came crying, saying that she was having a hard time. It turned out that the silver dollar was made of copper and could not be used. The old woman came to Zhong Desheng to ask him to exchange it, but Zhong deliberately cheated and insisted on not admitting it. The old woman originally wanted to make a profit from this, but she lost the shoes and also had to find change. She cried even more, but she didn't dare to argue with Zhong. I happened to pass by the door and asked about the reason. I understood in my heart and had to give the old woman one yuan, took the copper silver dollar, and put it in my pocket. This matter was considered over.

Not long after, the Jin-Feng War suddenly broke out. We were all ordered to go to the front. One day, I was commanding the troops to attack when a bullet flew straight towards my abdomen. At that time, I couldn't dodge, so I had to wait for death. But I was not harmed. I wondered why and looked closely. It turned out that the bullet had cleverly hit the copper silver dollar, turning it into a pot shape, so I was not injured. I remembered Zhong Desheng and checked the troops in the evening, only to find out that Zhong Desheng had died in battle long ago.

This story is what I personally experienced. I still keep that copper silver dollar to this day. Isn't this a clear manifestation of karma?

Tall Buildings 180

— Qiushui

Recently, someone is building a twenty-four-story tall building at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Park Road in Shanghai. It is said that after this building is completed, it will be the first in the world, except for the United States. At least in the Far East, it will definitely be the best. However, at the same time, there is news that a public house built by a foreign company on the banks of Suzhou Creek is eager to show off and has started building a high-rise building of more than twenty-four stories, vying for the top spot in the Far East. Human ambition and competitiveness are used in this kind of place. Crafts are thus developed, science is thus advanced, and world civilization is thus glorified and limitless.

In the United States, there is a similar situation, and the competition is even more fierce. Today I build a thirty-story building, and tomorrow you build a forty-story building. Novelty is seen every day, and patterns are endless. According to the current record, the newly opened hotel on Park Street in New York can be regarded as the tallest, most beautiful, and best building in the whole world in the United States. The hotel has 2,200 guest rooms. The equipment in each room, in addition to the usual ones, has a radio and a video receiver. The whole building soars into the clouds, reaching forty-seven stories. There is a light railway around the building, specially prepared for people in the hotel to patrol.

However, this hotel, as it stands, has already had its

moment. In the near future, it will have to step down and retire. Because the plan for the "Fashionable Building" has been completed in the same city and will soon begin construction. After this fashionable building is completed, not only will it increase the number of floors to sixty, knocking down that big hotel with one punch, but also add different colors to the exterior of the building with originality. The lowest floors will be yellow and gold, followed by blue, followed by green, followed by red gold, followed by purple. Soaring high-rise buildings have dozens of colors, magnificent and splendid. I wonder who can knock it down.

Epitaph of Mr. Li of Xinghua (Part 1) 181

— Chen Tianying

Mr. Li, named Xiang, styled Shenyan, came from a family in Xinghua, Jiangsu. From the Grand Scholar of the Zhongji Hall of the Ming Dynasty, with the posthumous title of Wending, seven generations to Mr. Li's father, named Mou. He suffered family misfortune in his youth and moved to the western suburbs of Yancheng, where he lived. He married Zhao and had two sons. Mr. Li was the second son. Mr. Li was born with intelligence and exceeded ordinary people. From the age of speech, he knew how to hold books, sitting and reciting, without stumbling. Many elders came to his door and asked to see him, praising him and calling him a broken treasure. His family was not wealthy, and his father used Confucianism to do business, disliking cunning and profiteering. He did many things, but none were successful. His family became poorer and poorer, to the point where he could not afford tuition. Mr. Li began to study the Spring and Autumn Annals with Mr. Shi of Jiangdu at the age of seventeen. He memorized and reviewed it from morning to night, accumulating knowledge and understanding. He often suffered from poor health, and sometimes his eyes frequently lost blood. He almost used up the oil for the lamp. There was a kind aunt, Xu Taimu, who lived in a famous residence in Yancheng, still a scholarly family. She had a rich collection of books. She pitied Mr. Li's poverty and illness and invited him to live in her house, providing him with medicine and food, and treating him well, so that he could complete his studies and achieve success. Mr. Li became more and more determined to improve himself, and his illness gradually subsided. He was able to read all of Xu's books, and his studies were completed. In his life, he was sharp-eyed and quick-thinking when reading, breaking through all obstacles. When he gained something, he immediately made a judgment, with a calm brow and a wise tail, and his words were naturally witty. In the past, he had managed and understood the classics and historical records, but he was especially proficient in the Selections of Refined Literature by Prince Zhaoming. He met the subtleties and side by side, grasping the essentials. He had accumulated a lot in his stomach, and his writing was naturally different. He rarely compared to the vastness of Cao Xue in the same era. He liked to praise the study of four pairs in his articles. The four Lius refer to the Han Zhi, Shi Shuo Xin Yu, Wen Xin Diao Long, and Shi Tong. Among the authors of the previous dynasty, only Zhi Fu and Wang's Shu Xue said that China does not hurt the embroidery, and the quality does not suffer from reality. How many people in ancient and modern times are elegant and lofty? He hid himself to compare himself to this. Mr. Li suffered the loss of his father at the age of twenty-two, and his career was so gloomy and worried that he became ill and collapsed. Mr. Li gave up his studies to take care of him, personally participating in menial tasks, with utmost sincerity and devotion, without wasting day and night. He left instructions to Mr. Li, do not give up reading, you must return to the old residence, revive the declining clan, and preserve our Li family, then you have taught your son. From then on, Mr. Li took his father's instructions to heart and increasingly questioned and learned diligently. Although he was trapped in a difficult situation, he still strove to be strong. He often blamed himself, did you forget the concern of the ancestors when they were dying? He felt sad as if he was carrying a wound for the rest of his life, which was his ultimate nature. After leaving Jiangnan, he traveled among famous officials and nobles, and his reputation became great. Outstanding people in the country competed to welcome him. Shen Yi of Jiaxing always praised Mr. Li as his guest whenever he saw him. This is Mr. Li, the master of the Jianghuai selection study. Wang Xiangqi of Xiangtan, with his talent and arrogance, despised Cao and others, but he treated Mr. Li's books and questions with unusual respect, not treating him the same as the common people.

Records of Ma Shuanglou (13) 182

— Master of Seeking Happiness Studio

In the second episode, they laughed and talked with a good teacher, and heard the bad news. The home was robbed, and they pitied each other. The room in the inn became a spring.

Our hometown is the worst place. It is located in the most remote and chaotic mountains. In recent years, I don't know how many bandits have gathered around. These leaders who pull the poles are exploited by Japanese ronin. Secretly provide them with money and firearms. Instigate them to disturb the local area. In order to give Japan an opportunity to advance and invade. They don't understand this. Sure enough, they gathered parties. At every turn, one or two thousand people or three to five hundred people is one pole. They ravaged our place and left no clean land. Either they robbed openly with fire. Or they kidnapped and extorted ransom. The people could not live in peace for half a day. I live in the county seat. There are still some troops and police guarding the city. More safe. His Anjiazhai is in the countryside. Bandits often went to harass them in groups. Later, all the villages and towns in the countryside saw that the government officials were out of reach. Unable to protect them. They jointly agreed on a method of self-defense. Each village and town organizes its own militia. Defend against bandits. Yutian's father, An, was a well-known gentleman in the local area. He is also the village chief of Anjiazhai. Then he was publicly elected as the chief of the militia. Speaking of this, I coughed occasionally. Liang Xiaoyun wanted to cut off his words because he was tired of listening. You're talking nonsense again. I'm in a hurry to ask what happened. Who is in the mood to listen to these things about bandits and militias. Wei Zhuomou also became anxious. Trees rise from the roots. Water flows to distant places. To talk about one thing. You have to explain the reasons in detail from the beginning. I didn't expect you to be so impatient. Then. I'll just say it simply and directly. Half a month ago. His father did not know for what reason. He offended a bandit leader named Niu Blackwind. Led a group of people into his Anjiazhai. Kill everyone you meet. Burn every house you see. His parents, both old, died under the random guns of the bandits. The entire village was washed clean. The houses were burned down. He also has a younger brother. His life and death are still unknown. Later, the government troops heard the news and went to help. The bandits tied up a lot of wealth. Kidnapped a few meat tickets. Before the government troops arrived, they roared away. Anjiazhai was only left with a pile of rubble and ashes, and even the funeral of the dead could not be arranged. You think Yutian received this bad news of family destruction. How painful must be in his heart. Do you have the leisure to come to you? This string of words. Like a string of arrows shooting non-stop. One branch after another directly pierced Liang Xiaoyun's fragile heart. Suddenly the ground collapsed. The flower-like face faded. The delicate red powder cheeks. Suddenly it turned pale like a layer of white paper. And it seems that the whole body limbs. They all fell into a freezing cold cellar. I couldn't help but feel a burst of chills. I couldn't help but tremble an jade hand. Holding Wei Zhuomou's arm tightly, he asked in a trembling voice. This… this is so scary. Didn't it ruin him alive? Now... what is he planning to do now?

Three Savings for National Salvation 183

A Western philosopher said, "China is a country that manufactures slogans." I think this statement contains at least 95% of the truth.

Look at the Northeast, from the provinces that were lost, until now, it has been more than three months. During these one hundred and more days, we, who are hanging the gilded signboard of resisting Japan and saving the country, have resisted what? Saved what? However, undoubtedly, we have only compiled a book of scriptures for saving the country.

There are many ways to save the country, each with its own ingenuity. Resisting Japan and saving the country is a wedge. Eighty-eight, sixty-four changes, there is the so-called "slogan to save the country," "black gauze to save the country." Therefore, the Eastern-made pins and paper in the cigarette paper store are sold out. The students think it is good to strike, so they all implement it, "strike to save the country." The professors think it is not good, and immediately shout to save the country without forgetting to study, and study without forgetting to save the country. "Studying to save the country" Modern men and women step up their work, compromise "You must pity me, and I pity you" "Love to save the country" Flower F of social interaction invented "Love letter to save the country." One call, hundreds of promises. The enthusiastic group implemented the "Armed to save the country" plan, so everywhere inside Shanhaiguan is a mixed army of bare hands.

The fascination of coffee shop beauty, the movement of flesh in the ballroom, the former is "Eating to save the country," the latter is "Dancing to save the country." The cinema emits a strong and dazzling Neon light. Batches of voyeurs stagger and disappear into its bloody mouth. It is said that this is "Entertainment to save the country" The bookstore owner rushed to print a large number of "beautiful cards" and published its "New Year to save the country" advertisement in the newspaper. In addition, adults have "Peace to save the country" and "Unification to save the country," artists have "Art to save the country," athletes have "Sports to save the country," economics doctors have "Cloth clothes to save the country" . . . . . .

"Save the country, save the country"! It has accomplished countless careers and created countless celebrities. It is precisely

The sound of saving the country fills the world,

Popular Literature

A Person Strolling on the Road 184

— Ding Nu

All day long he wanders on the road, carrying a load of oranges and sugarcane, peddling everywhere. Although he can only earn four or five corners a day, his family depends on this income to survive. He has been living this life for several years.

One day, he ran home in the evening with joy and said to his wife, "I had good luck today. I went to peddle in front of a school and almost sold out all the goods. I will definitely go to Pudong to buy some new goods tomorrow. Look!"

As he spoke, he took out all the money in his bag. The glittering of the white silver coins attracted his wife's attention. His wife smiled with satisfaction.

From this time on, he stood in front of the school every day to peddle.

X X X

About a year later, a bungalow was built in front of the school. A lot of fresh fruits were placed in front of the store, and various canned foods and cigarettes were placed on the shelves. Inside was a coffee shop. A group of students walked here after class to eat fruits and drink coffee. From morning to night, there was almost no empty seat inside. It was often possible to see people surrounding the front of the store. The business can be said to be very good.

At this time, everyone knew that the peddler who had been carrying a load on the road a year ago was now the owner of this bungalow.

The boss stood at the door of the store with a radiant face, nodding and smiling at the customers!

Not long after, a middle-aged woman was added here, with a plump figure and shiny black eyes, and a delicate and beautiful face, which made the boss reveal a lot of spring. It is said that this woman is the boss's newly married concubine. The boss is very lucky!

At that time, the boss's heart was blooming, and he often went out with his concubine. From this time on, he was rarely seen standing at the door of the store.

X X X

It was one afternoon three years later. The north wind was blowing, and the weather was very cold. There was almost no one walking on the road. At this time, a dung truck was pushed out from the school gate. It was full of residual vegetable juice, probably to feed the pigs. The person pushing the cart was sweating and pushing it from side to side, obviously he didn't have that much strength.

After he walked past, someone stood at the school gate and said:

"He is the owner of the fruit shop in that bungalow two years ago. Now he is in trouble."

Popular Science

The Mystery of the Orient and the Challenge of Science 185

Calcutta dispatch from the World Society: An Indian named Swami possesses extraordinary skills, capable of swallowing various universally known deadly poisons without any harm.

Recently, at the University of Calcutta, under extremely rigorous scientific supervision, he publicly demonstrated his abilities. He swallowed extremely poisonous potassium cyanide, as well as glass shards and nails, without any adverse reactions. After swallowing the poisons, doctors examined his stomach with X-rays, confirming they were indeed inside.

Sir Lyman, the eminent British scientist in charge of the experiment, stated that this poses a concrete challenge to all of modern science, saying, "I am completely bewildered by him."

Fountain Spring 186

Mr. Zhou's "Air-Compressed Tin Can" from the other day was a physics novelty; now, the "Fountain" is a chemistry novelty. However, both experiments rely on air pressure to produce these phenomena, so they can be considered two methods of demonstrating air pressure.

The structure of the "Fountain" is very simple: all you need is a glass bottle, a cup, a long glass tube, a rubber ball, a suction tube, a dry battery, two copper wires, and a cup of salt water. First, pierce two holes in the bottle's stopper, ready to insert the suction tube and the long tube. Then, fill the empty cup with red or another colored water, and also put some water in the suction tube. Next, connect the two copper wires to the two poles of the battery, and insert the other ends of the copper wires into the salt water (allowing current to pass through the salt water). Before long, the salt water will turn yellowish-green, then pour some of the green water into the bottle. Then, cover the bottle with the stopper. Afterwards, heat the bottle over a fire, and you will see water vapor gradually evaporating. When the green water is almost dry, immediately install the long tube and the suction tube, and turn the bottle upside down so that the other end of the long tube is immersed in the cup of red water.

At this point, the "Fountain" is complete. As long as you squeeze the rubber ball (attached to the suction tube), the red water in the cup will immediately rise up the tube, and at the top, it will spray out very quickly—it's really beautiful, just like a "Fountain"—until the red water in the cup is completely sprayed out, then it will stop.

The principle behind this novelty is very common. The green water is water containing hydrochloric acid (because it still contains Nash). When it is heated in the bottle, it turns into gas, driving out the air in the bottle, so that the bottle contains only a large amount of hydrochloric acid gas. Afterwards, when the rubber ball is squeezed, water is injected into the bottle through the suction tube. Because "hydrochloric acid gas is very soluble in water," the gas in the bottle immediately dissolves in the water, causing the inside of the bottle to become a vacuum, that is, the air pressure is reduced. Therefore, the red water in the cup, under the pressure of the surrounding air (the pressure per square inch is equal to fifteen pounds of force), rises into the bottle with lower pressure. In this way, a "Fountain" novelty is formed.

Corrections: In yesterday's "Dead Ashes Reborn" article, manganese dioxide, the character for "oxygen" was mistakenly written as the character for "gas"; potassium chlorate, the character for "chlorine" was mistakenly written as the character for "oxygen."

Southeast Northwest

Street Sketch on the Tram by Xian Jun 187

In order to deliver some books to the Shanghai Law School, I had to take a trip to Shanghai.

By the time I returned to Baoshan Road, it was already 6:05 PM. The No. 3 tram was packed with people!

To the right of a classmate sitting next to me, a villager who looked like a worker suddenly sat down. Because the crowd was so dense, his arms were folded on the shoulders of those on either side. Furthermore, because of the shaking of the tram, his arms were rubbing irregularly on the shoulders of those on either side. This aroused the anger of the classmate to my right!

He uttered a hateful sound, glaring at the villager, and viciously pressed his left arm under his own right arm. Only then did he look at the tabloid in his hand, as if his anger had subsided a little. The villager, of course, did not make a sound or resist in any way. But I saw it all and remembered it in my heart!

I thought: If someone also a proud college student was sitting next to him, how would he dare? And if a fashionable young lady were sitting next to him, how could he bear to do so?

Street Sociology

"No Renting Without Family" by Zi An 188

Such is Shanghai (Part One)

After the plan to set up a small-scale library was decided, the next day, I, Wei Xin, and Ze Pu went to select a library site—actually, just to rent two bungalows.

We walked along Henan Road. Before long, we spotted a "For Rent" sign. So, we stopped moving forward.

*Ding ding ding…* Wei Xin stepped forward and rang the doorbell. In less than a minute, a nanny, as fat as a pig, came out to open the door.

"What do you want?" the nanny asked, half-opening and half-closing the door.

"To see the house!" Wei Xin replied.

The house for rent was on the third floor. We went up and looked around, front and back, left and right. The rooms were not too big and not too small, with a bedroom and an office, and there was no lack of sunlight or air…it was just right for us. We went down to the living room, but there wasn't a single person in sight. So, Wei Xin shouted loudly:

"Hello!"…

A middle-aged woman, wearing short clothes, covered in powder, and with disheveled hair, came out. Wei Xin asked her:

"How much does your house cost?"

"Thirty-two yuan!"

We couldn't help but shake our heads and click our tongues.

"Do you have family?" Before we could even bargain, the middle-aged woman asked us this question.

"No!" Wei Xin replied to her.

"No family, no renting!" The middle-aged woman walked away with her hands on her hips…

So, we had no choice but to go to the second house.

We went to one house after another, running around for half the day. It wasn't that there weren't any houses, or that we didn't have enough money; the only reason was that we "didn't have family," and they "only rent to families"!

I felt that this was outrageous! Does not having a "woman" (family) mean you can't rent a house? At twelve o'clock (we left at eight o'clock in the morning), I came back and said angrily: "No way! I have to go rent one this afternoon! I don't believe you can't rent a house without a woman!…"

Wei Xin, who was experienced in Shanghai, heard my words and explained to me:

"It's not their fault! Indeed, many single men rent houses, and then leave without paying them! Their meaning is: as long as you have a family member, the man can run away, but the 'woman' can't run away!…so they feel relieved…that's how Shanghai people are!…"

I felt that Wei Xin's words made sense. At the same time, I finally understood:

"So that's how Shanghai people are!…no,

That's how Shanghai society is!…" Haha! Interesting!…

Shanghai Stories

Shanghai Stories (12) Compiled and Translated by Zhou Rong 189

The Success of X Bund

The Bund was originally a small path along the Huangpu River used by boatmen to pull ropes. When the Chinese government announced the first set of land management regulations for the concessions, it had already declared that this path used by the rope pullers should be preserved. It was stipulated that a thirty-foot space should be left between the buildings along the river and the riverbank, that is, the construction of buildings must be thirty feet away from the riverbank. Therefore, foreigners building houses had to drive piles into the section of the riverbank in front of the foundation and fill in that section of the road. This is the origin of the Bund, but at that time it was still a muddy and difficult road; now it has become an extremely beautiful place for strolling. One of the characteristics of Shanghai now is that there is a very wide open space between the buildings facing the river and the riverbank. The original intention of preserving this wide open space was not for aesthetic reasons, but to leave a large road for boatmen to pull ropes.

Market News 190

Letter from Da Zhong Industrial Company: The waterproof silk fabric produced by Da Zhong Industrial Company has been rushed to manufacture by the company. It is sold by Minyi Socks Factory at Touji Bridge, Zhejiang Road, and Tong Kangxiang Foreign Goods Store at the intersection of Wusong Road and Minhang Road. This silk fabric has no abnormality in appearance compared to ordinary products, but in fact, it is impermeable to water. Also, it is as soft as before. If made into clothes, it can also be used to defend against rain.

Letter from Civilization Bookstore: Our country's medical books have always lacked good versions. Recently, the Shanghai National Medicine Research Society has compiled and printed "Crystallization in Three Sections of National Medicine: Diagnosis, Pathology, and Drugs," which selects materials appropriately and focuses on practical use. It is now sold by the Shanghai Nanjing Road Civilization Bookstore, and medical circles generally praise it as a good book.
